# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Migration Guide: Envoy External Processing Filter (v1.30 → v1.31)

## Task

Generate a comprehensive migration guide for upgrading the Envoy External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter from **version 1.30.0 to version 1.31.0**.

## Context

The workspace contains two versions of the Envoy codebase:
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.30/` - Envoy v1.30.0 (April 2024)
- `/workspace/envoy-v1.31/` - Envoy v1.31.0 (July 2024)

## Scope

Focus specifically on the **External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter** configuration and implementation changes. This filter allows external services to process HTTP requests and responses.

Your migration guide should identify and document:

1. **Breaking Changes** - Incompatible configuration or behavioral changes
2. **Deprecated Features** - Fields or modes marked for future removal
3. **New Features** - Added capabilities and configuration options
4. **Configuration Updates** - Required or recommended changes to ext_proc filter configuration
5. **Behavioral Changes** - Modifications to filter behavior or runtime semantics

## Relevant Components

The ext_proc filter is primarily located in:
- Proto definitions: `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/`
- Implementation: `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/`
- Documentation: `docs/root/configuration/http/http_filters/ext_proc_filter.rst`

## Deliverable

Write your migration guide to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format with the following sections:

1. **Overview** - Summary of the migration and major changes
2. **Breaking Changes** - Critical incompatible changes requiring action
3. **Deprecated Features** - Features marked for deprecation with migration advice
4. **New Features** - New capabilities and how to use them
5. **Migration Steps** - Step-by-step instructions for upgrading configurations
6. **Testing Recommendations** - How to validate the migration
7. **Rollback Guidance** - How to revert if issues occur

## Requirements

- Provide specific proto field names and types
- Include before/after configuration examples for each breaking change
- Explain the motivation or benefit behind major changes
- Cite specific source files where implementations changed
- Recommend best practices for adopting new features
- Identify common migration pitfalls or edge cases

## Tips

- Compare the two version directories to identify changed proto fields and implementation files
- Search for all API modifications in the ext_proc filter
- Trace configuration usage patterns across both versions
- Look for related documentation updates

The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference pa
... (truncated)

The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n12: \n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n14: external processor\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n18: messages.\n19: \n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\n26: \n27: This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n28: are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n29: be found on the :ref:`reference pa
... (truncated)

155-assistanttext-
The migration guide has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here is a summary of what was found and documented:

## Key Findings

**Breaking Change:**
- `ImmediateResponse.body` in `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto` changed from `string` to `bytes`. Ext_proc servers that set this field must update generated stubs and code. Wire encoding is compatible, but typed languages will require recompilation.

**Deprecated Feature:**
- `disable_clear_route_cache` (bool, field 11) is annotated for future promotion into a `oneof` group. It is superseded by the new `route_cache_action` enum field. Setting both simultaneously is not allowed.

**New Features:**
1. **`route_cache_action`** (field 18) — a 3-value enum (`DEFAULT`/`CLEAR`/`RETAIN`) on `ExternalProcessor` that replaces the coarser `disable_clear_route_cache` boolean with finer-grained control.
2. **`deferred_close_timeout`** (field 19) — controls how long Envoy holds open gRPC streams in `observability_mode` after an HTTP transaction completes. Default: 5 seconds.
3. **Observability mode** fully implemented — includes `ThreadLocalStreamManager`, deferred stream cleanup, and `sendHeadersInObservabilityMode`/`sendDataInObservabilityMode` helpers.

**Behavioral Changes:**
- Ext_proc message timeouts now return **504 Gateway Timeout** (was 500).
- gRPC tracing context headers are now propagated to the ext_proc service.

[#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n24: // External Processing Filter\\n25: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n26: \\n27: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n28: \\n29: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n30: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n31: //\\n32: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n33: \\n34: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n35: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n36: //\\n37: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n39: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n40: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n41: //\\n42: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n43: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n44: // and how it should be processed.\\n45: //\\n46: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n47: //\\n48: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n49: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n50: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n51: //   sent asynchronously.\\n52: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n53: //\\n54: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n55: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n56: // processor must send a matching response.\\n57: //\\n58: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n59: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n60: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n61: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n62: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n63: //   to SEND.\\n64: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n65: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n66: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n67: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n68: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n69: //   request trailers.\\n70: //\\n71: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n72: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n73: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n74: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n75: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n76: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n77: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n78: //\\n79: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n80: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n81: //\\n82: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n83: //   on the content of the headers.\\n84: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n85: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n86: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n87: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n88: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n89: //\\n90: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\\n23: \\n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\\n25: // External Processing Filter\\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\\n27: \\n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\\n29: \\n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\\n32: //\\n33: // * \\\"async mode\\\" is not implemented.\\n34: \\n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \\\"external processor\\\"\\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\\n37: //\\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\\n42: //\\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\\n45: // and how it should be processed.\\n46: //\\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\\n48: //\\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\\n54: //\\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\\n58: //\\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\\n64: //   to SEND.\\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\\n70: //   request trailers.\\n71: //\\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\\n79: //\\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\\n82: //\\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\\n90: //\\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n92: // server\\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\\n96: //\\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\\n99: // name.\\n100: //\\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\\n110: \\n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n112:     // the external processor response.\\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\\n114: \\n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\\n116:     // the external processor response. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\\n234:   //\\n235:   // .. warning::\\n236:   //\\n237:   //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\\n238:   //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\\n239:   //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\\n240:   //    discretion when enabling this feature.\\n241:   //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\\n242:   //\\n243:   bool observability_mode = 17;\\n244: \\n245:   // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\\n246:   // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\\n247:   // field is set in an external processor response.\\n248:   // Only one of ``disable_clear_route_cache`` or ``route_cache_action`` can be set.\\n249:   // It is recommended to set ``route_cache_action`` which supersedes ``disable_clear_route_cache``.\\n250:   bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\\n251:       [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \\\"clear_route_cache_type\\\"];\\n252: \\n253:   // Specifies the action to be taken when an external processor response is\\n254:   // received in response to request headers. Currently, the deferred stream closure\\n261:   // is only used in :ref:`observability_mode <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.observability_mode>`.\\n262:   // In observability mode, gRPC streams may be held open to the external processor longer than the lifetime of the regular client to\\n263:   // backend stream lifetime. In this case, Envoy will eventually timeout the external processor stream according to this time limit.\\n264:   // The default value is 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds) if not specified.\\n265:   google.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\\n266: }\\n267: \\n268: // The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\\n269: // dynamic metadata. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\\n290:   // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\\n291:   MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\\n292: }\\n293: \\n294: // The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\\n295: // allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\\n296: //\\n297: // This works as below:\\n298: //\\n299: //   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\\n300: //   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\\n301: //      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n302: //   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\\n303: //      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\\n304: //   4.     "content": "1: syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\n6: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n7: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\n8: import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n9: import \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n10: \n11: import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n12: import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n13: \n14: import \"udpa/annotations/migrate.proto\";\n15: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n16: import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n17: \n18: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n19: option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\n21: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n23: \n24: // [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n25: // External Processing Filter\n26: // [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n27: \n28: // The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n29: \n30: // **Current Implementation Status:**\n31: // All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n32: //\n33: // * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n34: \n35: // The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n36: // that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n37: //\n38: // * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n39: // * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n40: // * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n41: // * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n42: //\n43: // The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n44: // request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n45: // and how it should be processed.\n46: //\n47: // By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n48: //\n49: // * Whether it receives the response message at all\n50: // * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n51: // * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n52: //   sent asynchronously.\n53: // * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n54: //\n55: // The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n56: // a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n57: // processor must send a matching response.\n58: //\n59: // * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n60: // * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n61: //   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n62: //   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n63: // * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n64: //   to SEND.\n65: // * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n66: //   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n67: //   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n68: // * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n69: // * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n70: //   request trailers.\n71: //\n72: // By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n73: // This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n74: // setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n75: // from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n76: // set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n77: // in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n78: // the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n79: //\n80: // All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n81: // sophisticated ways. For example:\n82: //\n83: // * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n84: //   on the content of the headers.\n85: // * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n86: //   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n87: // * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n88: //   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n89: //   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n90: //\n91: // The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n92: // server\n93: // :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n94: // messages, and the server must reply with\n95: // :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n96: //\n97: // Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n98: // <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n99: // name.\n100: //\n101: // [#next-free-field: 20]\n102: message ExternalProcessor {\n103:   // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n104:   // is received in response to request headers.\n105:   enum RouteCacheAction {\n106:     // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n107:     // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n108:     // field is set in an external processor response.\n109:     DEFAULT = 0;\n110: \n111:     // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n112:     // the external processor response.\n113:     CLEAR = 1;\n114: \n115:     // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n116:     // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n117:     // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n118:     // to true.\n119:     RETAIN = 2;\n120:   }\n121: \n122:   reserved 4;\n123: \n124:   reserved \"async_mode\";\n125: \n126:   // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n127:   // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n128:   config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n129: \n130:   // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n131:   // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n132:   // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n133:   // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n134:   // downstream client will be reset.\n135:   // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n136:   // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n137:   bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n138: \n139:   // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n140:   // sent. Envoy sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n29: // 2. The service sends back a ProcessingResponse message that directs Envoy\n30: //    to either stop processing, continue without it, or send it the\n31: //    next chunk of the message body.\n32: // 3. If so requested, Envoy sends the server chunks of the message body,\n33: //    or the entire body at once. In either case, the server sends back\n34: //    a ProcessingResponse after each message it receives.\n35: // 4. If so requested, Envoy sends the server the HTTP trailers,\n36: //    and the server sends back a ProcessingResponse.\n37: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again\n38: //    at step 1 when Envoy receives a response from the upstream server.\n39: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly,\n40: //    then Envoy proceeds without consulting the server.\n41: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error,\n42: //    then Envoy returns a 500 error to the client, unless the filter\n43: //    was configured to ignore errors.\n44: //\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but\n46: // using a gRPC stream to make it easier for the server to\n47: // maintain state.\n48: \n49: service ExternalProcessor {\n50:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that Envoy will use to\n51:   // give the server control over what the filter does. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\\n10: it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\\n11: and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\\n12: \\n13: The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\\n14: external processor\\n15: :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\\n16: messages, and the processor must reply with\\n17: :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\\n18: messages.\\n19: \\n20: Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\\n21: This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\\n22: request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\\n23: on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\\n24: that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\\n25: stream requests from the proxy.\\n26: \\n27: This filter is a work in progress. With this change the destructor can be called on any thread.\\n7:     This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag ``envoy.reloadable_features.allow_slot_destroy_on_worker_threads``\\n8:     to ``false``.\\n9: - area: ext_proc\\n10:   change: |\\n11:     Adding support for\\n12:     :ref:`route_cache_action <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.route_cache_action>`.\\n13:     It specifies the route action to be taken when an external processor response is received in response to request headers.\\n14: - area: http2\\n15:   change: |\\n16:     Changes the default value of ``envoy.reloadable_features.http2_use_oghttp2`` to ``true``. This changes the codec used for HTTP/2\\n17:     requests and responses. This behavior can be reverted by setting the feature to ``false``.\\n18: - area: http3\\n19:   change: |\\n20:     Added a happy eyeballs feature to HTTP/3 upstream, where it assuming happy eyeballs sorting results in alternating address\\n21:     families will attempt the first v4 and v6 address before giving up on HTTP/3.  This change can be reverted by setting\\n22:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.http3_happy_eyeballs`` to ``false``.\\n23: - area: http2\\n24:   change: |\\n25:     Passes HTTP/2 ``DATA`` frames through a different codec API. This behavior can be temporarily disabled by setting the runtime\\n26:     feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.http2_use_visitor_for_data`` to ``false``.\\n27: - area: runtime\\n28:   change: |\\n29:     Rejecting invalid YAML. The tokens will be refilled when\\n55:     the token bucket is accessed and no dependency on the timer.\\n56:     This behavior can be temporarily reverted by setting the runtime guard\\n57:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.no_timer_based_rate_limit_token_bucket`` to ``false``.\\n58: \\n59: minor_behavior_changes:\\n60: - area: ext_proc\\n61:   change: |\\n62:     Timeout errors in external processor now returns ``504 Gateway Timeout`` to downstream clients.\\n63:     The previous behavior was returning ``500 Internal Server Error``.\\n64: - area: dfp\\n65:   change: |\\n66:     Changed dynamic forward proxy so local reply errors include DNS resolution details. Previously, tracing context headers\\n73:     were not being set when calling external services such as ext_proc.\\n74: - area: http\\n75:   change: |\\n76:     Fixed host header changes for shadow requests to properly handle ipv6 addresses.\\n77: - area: tracers\\n78:   change: |\\n79:     Set status code for OpenTelemetry tracers (previously unset).\\n80: - area: config\\n81:   change: |\\n82:     Stricter validation of a ``google.protobuf.Duration`` field in a config, rejecting invalid values (where the number\\n83:     of years is over 292). This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag\\n89:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.xdstp_path_avoid_colon_encoding`` to ``false``.\\n90: - area: udp\\n91:   change: |\\n92:     Change GRO read buffer to 64kB to avoid ``MSG_TRUNC``. This behavior can be temporarily disabled by setting\n31:     the runtime feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.reject_invalid_yaml`` to ``false`` but the runtime guard must be\n32:     parsed before any invalid YAML.\n33: - area: proxy_protocol\n34:   change: |\n35:     Populate typed metadata by default in proxy protocol listener. Typed metadata can be consumed as\n36:     :ref:`TlvsMetadata type <envoy_v3_api_msg_data.core.v3.TlvsMetadata>`.\n37:     This change can be temporarily disabled by setting the runtime flag\n38:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.use_typed_metadata_in_proxy_protocol_listener`` to ``false``.\n39: - area: composite_filter\n40:   change: |\n41:     Adding support for\n42:     :ref:`sample_percent <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.composite.v3.ExecuteFilterAction.sample_percent>`.\n43:     It specifies the probability of the action execution. If not specified, it is 100%.\n44: - area: golang\n45:   change: |\n46:     Move ``Continue``, ``SendLocalReply`` and ``RecoverPanic`` from ``FilterCallbackHandler`` to ``DecoderFilterCallbacks`` and\n47:     ``EncoderFilterCallbacks``, to support full-duplex processing.\n48: - area: tracing/datadog\n49:   change: |\n50:     Disabled remote configuration by default.\n51:     To enable this feature, use the :ref:`remote_config <envoy_v3_api_field_config.trace.v3.DatadogConfig.remote_config>` field.\n52: - area: local_ratelimit\n53:   change: |\n54:     Updated the token bucket implementation to use non-timer based token bucket. Previously, tracing context headers\n73:     were not being set when calling external services such as ext_proc.\n74: - area: http\n75:   change: |\n76:     Fixed host header changes for shadow requests to properly handle ipv6 addresses.\n77: - area: tracers\n78:   change: |\n79:     Set status code for OpenTelemetry tracers (previously unset).\n80: - area: config\n81:   change: |\n82:     Stricter validation of a ``google.protobuf.Duration`` field in a config, rejecting invalid values (where the number\n83:     of years is over 292). This can be temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard\n84:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.strict_duration_validation`` to ``false``.\n85: - area: xds\n86:   change: |\n87:     Updated xDS-TP path naming to better comply with RFC-3986. This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag\n89:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.xdstp_path_avoid_colon_encoding`` to ``false``.\n90: - area: udp\n91:   change: |\n92:     Change GRO read buffer to 64kB to avoid ``MSG_TRUNC``. This change brings the behavior in line with\n186:     the documentation.\n187: - area: outlier detection\n188:   change: |\n189:     Fixed :ref:`successful_active_health_check_uneject_host\n190:     <envoy_v3_api_field_config.cluster.v3.OutlierDetection.successful_active_health_check_uneject_host>`.\n191:     Before, a failed health check could uneject the host if the ``FAILED_ACTIVE_HC`` health flag had not been set.\n192: - area: quic\n193:   change: |\n194:     Applied 2 QUICHE patches for crash bugs in ``QuicSpdyStream`` ``OnDataAvailable()`` and ``OnInitialHeaderComplete()``.\n195: - area: quic\n196:   change: |\n197:     Fixed crash bug when QUIC downstream stream was read closed and then timed out.\n198: - area: tls\n199:   change: |\n200:     Fix a ``RELEASE_ASSERT`` when using :ref:`auto_sni <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.UpstreamHttpProtocolOptions.auto_sni>`\n201:     if the downstream request ``:authority`` was longer than 255 characters.\n202: - area: tracing\n203:   change: |\n204:     Fix an issue where span id is missing from OpenTelemetry access log entries.\n205: - area: ext_authz\n206:   change: |\n207:     Added field\n208:     :ref:`validate_mutations <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_authz.v3.ExtAuthz.validate_mutations>`,\n209:     which, when set to ``true``, adds header and query parameter mutation validation to the HTTP ext_authz\n210:     filter. If an authz response contains invalid mutations, the filter responds to the downstream\n211:     request with HTTP ``500 Internal Server Error``. If you use ext_authz with an untrusted side stream,\n212:     it's recommended you set this to ``true``.\n213: - area: http\n214:   change: |\n215:     Fix a crash when reloading the HTTP Connection Manager via ECDS.\n216: - area: cares\n217:   change: |\n218:     Upgraded c-ares library to 1.20.1 and added fix to c-ares DNS implementation to additionally check for ``ARES_EREFUSED``,\n219:     ``ARES_ESERVFAIL`` and ``ARES_ENOTIMP`` status. Without this fix, ``DestroyChannelOnRefused`` and\n220:     ``CustomResolverValidAfterChannelDestruction`` unit test will break.\n221: - area: udp\n222:   change: |\n223:     Fixed a bug that would cause Envoy to crash when updates to a pre-existing cluster were made (e.g. ``HostSet`` changes).\n224: - area: ext_authz\n225:   change: |\n226:     Handle ``append_action`` from :ref:`external authorization service <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.auth.v3.CheckResponse>`\n227:     that was ignored.\n228: - area: oauth2\n229:   change: |\n230:     Fixed a bug that would cause Envoy to crash when receiving an Oauth callback while the Oauth upstream is unhealthy\n231:     (e.g. due to DNS issues).\n232: - area: http\n233:   change: |\n234:     Fix BalsaParser resetting state too early, guarded by\n235:     ``envoy.reloadable_features.http1_balsa_delay_reset`` which defaults to ``true``.\n236: - area: ext_authz\n237:   change: |\n238:     Set the SNI value from the requested server name if it isn't available on the connection/socket. This applies when\n239:     ``include_tls_session`` is ``true``. The requested server name is set on a connection when filters such as the TLS\n240:     inspector are used.\n241: - area: oauth\n242:   change: |\n243:     The ID token cookie now expires at the same time the id token itself expires, instead of when the access token expires.\n244: - area: decompression\n245:   change: |\n246:     Fixed a bug where Envoy will go into an endless loop when using the brotli decompressor. If the input stream has\n247:     redundant data, the decompressor will loop forever.\n248: - area: websocket\n249:   change: |\n250:     Only ``101`` is considered a successful response for websocket handshake for HTTP/1.1, and Envoy as a proxy will proxy the response\n251:     header from upstream to downstream and then close the request if other status is received. This behavior can be\n252:     reverted by ``envoy_reloadable_features_check_switch_protocol_websocket_handshake``.\n253: - area: async http client\n254:   change: |\n255:     Added one option to disable the response body buffering for mirror request. Also introduced a 32MB cap for the response\n256:     buffer, which can be changed by the runtime flag ``http.async_response_buffer_limit`` based on the product needs.\n257: - area: ext_authz\n258:   change: |\n259:     Validate http service\n260:     :ref:`path_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_authz.v3.HttpService.path_prefix>`,\n261:     Valid HTTP service ``path_prefix`` configuration must start with ``/``.\n262: - area: local_ratelimit\n263:   change: |\n264:     Fixed a bug where the local rate limit filter would crash when the\n265:     :ref:`enable_x_ratelimit_headers <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ratelimit.v3.RateLimit>`\n266:     is set to ``DRAFT_VERSION_03`` and a send local reply is triggered before the rate limit filter is executed.\n267: - area: admin\n268:   change: |\n269:     Fixed missing :ref:`additional addresses <envoy_v3_api_msg_config.endpoint.v3.Endpoint.AdditionalAddress>`\n270:     for :ref:`LbEndpoint <envoy_v3_api_field_config.endpoint.v3.LbEndpoint.endpoint>` in config dump.\n271: - area: tracing\n272:   change: |\n273:     Added support to configure a static config resource detector for the OpenTelemetry tracer.\n274: - area: http\n275:   change: |\n276:     Fixed a bug where additional :ref:`cookie attributes <envoy_v3_api_msg_config.route.v3.RouteAction.HashPolicy.cookie>`\n277:     are not sent properly to clients.\n278: - area: datadog\n279:   change: |\n280:     Bumped the version of datadog to resolve a crashing bug in earlier versions of the library.\n281: - area: lua\n282:   change: |\n283:     Fixed a bug where the user data will reference a dangling pointer to the Lua state and cause a crash.\n284: \n285: removed_config_or_runtime:\n286: - area: tls\n287:   change: |\n288:     Removed ``envoy.reloadable_features.enable_intermediate_ca`` runtime flag and lagacy code paths.\n289: - area: oauth\n290:   change: |\n291:     Removed ``envoy.reloadable_features.oauth_use_standard_max_age_value`` runtime flag and lagacy code paths.\n292: -   "content": "# Envoy ext_proc HTTP Filter: Migration Guide v1.30 \u2192 v1.31\n\n## Overview\n\nEnvoy v1.31.0 (released July 19, 2024) introduces several meaningful changes to the External Processing (ext_proc) HTTP filter. The changes fall into three categories:\n\n1. **A breaking API type change** in the `ImmediateResponse` message (`body` field: `string` \u2192 `bytes`)\n2. **New configuration fields** on `ExternalProcessor` for route cache control and observability stream lifecycle management\n3. **Behavioral changes** affecting timeout error codes and gRPC tracing propagation\n\nThe `processing_mode.proto` file is unchanged between the two versions.\n\n**Source files examined:**\n- `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n- `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`\n- `source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h`\n- `changelogs/current.yaml` (v1.31.0)\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Changes\n\n### 1. `ImmediateResponse.body` type changed from `string` to `bytes`\n\n**File:** `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`, field `ImmediateResponse.body` (field number 3)\n\n**v1.30.0:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  string body = 3;   // <-- was string\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n**v1.31.0:**\n```protobuf\nmessage ImmediateResponse {\n  type.v3.HttpStatus status = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n  HeaderMutation headers = 2;\n  bytes body = 3;    // <-- now bytes\n  GrpcStatus grpc_status = 4;\n  string details = 5;\n}\n```\n\n**Impact:** Any ext_proc server implementation that populates the `body` field of `ImmediateResponse` must be updated. In most gRPC code-generation ecosystems the wire format of `string` and `bytes` is identical (both are length-delimited), so existing Protobuf-serialized messages will still decode without error. However:\n\n- **Generated code in typed languages** (Go, Java, C++, Python with strict typing) will produce a compile or runtime type error if the field is accessed as `string` after regenerating the stubs from the new proto.\n- **Dynamic languages or JSON serialization paths** may experience encoding differences (JSON represents `bytes` as base64, whereas `string` is a plain JSON string).\n\n**Why the change?** The `body` field carries raw HTTP response body bytes, which may contain arbitrary binary data (e.g., compressed or binary content). Using `string` was incorrect because protobuf `string` requires valid UTF-8, whereas `bytes` accepts arbitrary byte sequences.\n\n**Migration action:**\n\n1. Regenerate your gRPC stubs from the v1.31 proto definitions.\n2. Update your ext_proc server code to construct the `ImmediateResponse.body` as a byte array/slice rather than a string.\n\n**Before (Go example):**\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &v3.HttpStatus{Code: v3.StatusCode_Forbidden},\n    Body:   \"Access denied\",  // string\n}\n```\n\n**After (Go example):**\n```go\nresp := &ext_proc.ImmediateResponse{\n    Status: &v3.HttpStatus{Code: v3.StatusCode_Forbidden},\n    Body:   []byte(\"Access denied\"),  // bytes\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Deprecated Features\n\n### 1. `disable_clear_route_cache` superseded by `route_cache_action`\n\n**File:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\nThe existing boolean field `disable_clear_route_cache` (field 11) is now annotated with a migration hint indicating it will be promoted into a `oneof` group (`clear_route_cache_type`) alongside the new `route_cache_action` field. The documentation comment in v1.31 explicitly states:\n\n> \"It is recommended to set `route_cache_action` which supersedes `disable_clear_route_cache`. Only one of `disable_clear_route_cache` or `route_cache_action` can be set.\"\n\n**v1.30.0:**\n```protobuf\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n```\n\n**v1.31.0:**\n```protobuf\nbool disable_clear_route_cache = 11\n    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18\n    [(udpa.annotations.field_migrate).oneof_promotion = \"clear_route_cache_type\"];\n```\n\nThe `disable_clear_route_cache = true` configuration is equivalent to setting `route_cache_action = RETAIN`. Setting both fields simultaneously is not permitted.\n\n**Migration advice:** Replace `disable_clear_route_cache: true` with `route_cache_action: RETAIN` in your filter configuration. Remove `disable_clear_route_cache` from any configuration that also sets `route_cache_action`.\n\n---\n\n## New Features\n\n### 1. New `RouteCacheAction` enum on `ExternalProcessor`\n\n**File:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`\n\nA new enum `RouteCacheAction` and corresponding field `route_cache_action` (field 18) provide finer-grained control over route cache behavior when request headers are processed by the external processor.\n\n```protobuf\nenum RouteCacheAction {\n  // Clear the route cache only when clear_route_cache is set in the ext_proc response (default).\n  DEFAULT = 0;\n\n  // Always clear the route cache, regardless of the clear_route_cache bit.\n  CLEAR = 1;\n\n  // Never clear the route cache, regardless of the clear_route_cache bit.\n  // Equivalent to disable_clear_route_cache = true.\n  RETAIN = 2;\n}\n\nRouteCacheAction route_cache_action = 18;\n```\n\n**Example configuration (YAML):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      # New: always clear the route cache after processing request headers\n      route_cache_action: CLEAR\n```\n\n**When to use each value:**\n- `DEFAULT` \u2014 Keep existing behaviour; the external processor signals when to clear the cache via the `clear_route_cache` field in its response.\n- `CLEAR` \u2014 Use when your ext_proc server always modifies routing headers (e.g., `:authority`, `x-forwarded-host`) and you want to guarantee the route is re-evaluated.\n- `RETAIN` \u2014 Use when you want to prevent route re-evaluation even if the ext_proc server requests it (e.g., for security or performance reasons). Replaces `disable_clear_route_cache: true`.\n\n**Behavioral note (changelog):** Adding `route_cache_action` is recorded as a *behavior change* in the v1.31 changelog, meaning its introduction actively changes how configurations that had `disable_clear_route_cache` are interpreted and encouraged to migrate.\n\n---\n\n### 2. New `deferred_close_timeout` field on `ExternalProcessor`\n\n**File:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`, field 19\n\n```protobuf\n// Specifies the deferred closure timeout for the gRPC stream that connects to the external\n// processor. Currently used only in observability_mode.\n// Default: 5000 milliseconds (5 seconds).\ngoogle.protobuf.Duration deferred_close_timeout = 19;\n```\n\nThis field controls how long Envoy holds open an observability-mode gRPC stream after the client-to-backend stream has completed. In observability mode, the ext_proc gRPC stream may outlive the regular HTTP transaction (because the ext_proc server does not respond to each message). This timeout prevents streams from being held open indefinitely.\n\n**Default:** 5000 ms (5 seconds). Introduced alongside the `observability_mode` feature; if you use `observability_mode: true`, consider tuning this value based on your ext_proc server's processing latency.\n\n**Example configuration (YAML):**\n```yaml\nhttp_filters:\n  - name: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc\n    typed_config:\n      \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n      grpc_service:\n        envoy_grpc:\n          cluster_name: ext_proc_cluster\n      observability_mode: true\n      deferred_close_timeout: \"10s\"  # Hold streams open up to 10 seconds\n```\n\n---\n\n### 3. `observability_mode` formally supported with deferred stream lifecycle management\n\n**File:** `api/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/ext_proc.proto`, field 17 (present in v1.30); implementation infrastructure added in v1.31\n\nThe `observability_mode` field existed in v1.30 but in v1.31 received full implementation support including:\n\n- A new `ThreadLocalStreamManager` class (`source/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/ext_proc.h`) that tracks active observability-mode streams across threads.\n- A new `DeferredDeletableStream` struct that wraps the gRPC stream and closes it after `deferred_close_timeout` elapses.\n- The `encodeComplete()` callback now calls `logGrpcStreamInfo()` in observability mode.\n- Helper methods `sendHeadersInObservabilityMode()` and `sendDataInObservabilityMode()` were added to the `Filter` class.\n\nThe changelog entry for this feature states:\n\n> \"Added support for observability mode which deprecates `async_mode`. If enabled, each part of the HTTP request or response specified by `ProcessingMode` is sent without waiting for the response from the ext_proc service. It is 'Send and Go' mode that can be used by external processor to observe Envoy data and status.\"\n\n**In observability mode (v1.31 behavior):**\n1. Only `STREAMED` body processing mode is supported; other body modes are ignored.\n2. The ext_proc server must not send back processing responses; responses are silently ignored.\n3. The `message_timeout` restriction does not apply.\n4. The ext_proc server may close the stream to indicate no more messages are needed.\n5. After the HTTP transaction completes, Envoy holds the gRPC stream open for up to `deferred_close_timeout`.\n\n---\n\n## Behavioral Changes\n\n### 1. Timeout errors now return `504 Gateway Timeout` instead of `500 Internal Server Error`\n\n**Area:** `ext_proc` (changelog `minor_behavior_changes`)\n\nWhen the ext_proc message timeout fires (controlled by `message_timeout`), Envoy previously returned `500 Internal Server Error` to the downstream client. As of v1.31.0, it returns `504 Gateway Timeout`.\n\n**Impact:** Downstream clients or monitoring systems that inspect HTTP status codes to differentiate between internal errors and gateway timeouts will observe this change automatically. No configuration change is required, but you should update:\n- Alert rules that trigger on `500` errors specifically for ext_proc timeouts.\n- Integration tests that assert a specific response code when ext_proc times out.\n\n---\n\n### 2. gRPC tracing context headers are now propagated in ext_proc streams\n\n**Area:** `grpc` / `ext_proc` (changelog `minor_behavior_changes`)\n\nPreviously, tracing context headers (e.g., `traceparent`, `x-b3-traceid`) were not propagated when calling the ext_proc external service via either the Envoy gRPC client or the Google gRPC client. As of v1.31.0, these headers are correctly propagated.\n\n**Impact:** If you use distributed tracing (Zipkin, Jaeger, OpenTelemetry, Datadog), ext_proc calls will now appear as child spans in traces. This is generally desirable. However, be aware that:\n- Your ext_proc server will now receive tracing headers it previously did not see.\n- If your ext_proc server forwards requests upstream, it should propagate these headers to maintain trace continuity.\n\n---\n\n## Migration Steps\n\nFollow these steps in order when upgrading from Envoy v1.30.0 to v1.31.0:\n\n### Step 1: Update `ImmediateResponse.body` in your ext_proc server\n\n1. Regenerate gRPC stubs from the updated proto files (specifically `api/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3/external_processor.proto`).\n2. Update all code that sets `ImmediateResponse.body` to use `bytes` instead of `string`.\n3. If you serialize `ImmediateResponse` to JSON (e.g., for logging or testing), update your deserialization logic to handle the field as base64-encoded bytes rather than a plain UTF-8 string.\n\n### Step 2: Migrate `disable_clear_route_cache` to `route_cache_action`\n\nReplace:\n```yaml\n# v1.30 configuration\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  disable_clear_route_cache: true\n```\n\nWith:\n```yaml\n# v1.31 recommended configuration\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  route_cache_action: RETAIN\n```\n\nIf you were using `disable_clear_route_cache: false` (or omitting it, since `false` is the default), no change is needed \u2014 that maps to `route_cache_action: DEFAULT`, which is also the default.\n\n**Important:** Do not set both `disable_clear_route_cache` and `route_cache_action` simultaneously. The proto annotations (`oneof_promotion`) indicate these fields are mutually exclusive.\n\n### Step 3: Configure `deferred_close_timeout` if using observability mode\n\nIf you use `observability_mode: true`, add a `deferred_close_timeout` appropriate for your workload:\n\n```yaml\ntyped_config:\n  \"@type\": type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor\n  observability_mode: true\n  deferred_close_timeout:\n    seconds: 10   # Adjust based on ext_proc processing latency\n```\n\nIf you do not set this field, the default of 5 seconds applies.\n\n### Step 4: Update monitoring for timeout error codes\n\n- Update any dashboards, alerts, or SLO definitions that distinguish `500` errors caused by ext_proc timeouts. These will now appear as `504` errors.\n- Update integration tests that check for specific HTTP status codes when simulating ext_proc timeout scenarios.\n\n### Step 5: Verify tracing integration\n\n- If you use distributed tracing, deploy the upgraded Envoy and verify in your tracing backend that ext_proc gRPC calls now appear correctly as child spans.\n- Confirm that your ext_proc server correctly handles and forwards the incoming tracing headers (e.g., `traceparent`, `x-b3-traceid`, `x-b3-spanid`).\n\n---\n\n## Testing Recommendations\n\n### Unit and Integration Tests\n\n1. **`ImmediateResponse.body` type check:** Write a test that sends an `ImmediateResponse` with binary content (non-UTF-8 bytes) in the `body` field. Verify Envoy correctly returns that binary content in the HTTP response body.\n\n2. **Route cache action:** Test all three `RouteCacheAction` values:\n   - `DEFAULT`: Verify the route is re-evaluated only when `clear_route_cache: true` is set in the response.\n   - `CLEAR`: Verify the route is always re-evaluated after request header processing, even if `clear_route_cache` is not set.\n   - `RETAIN`: Verify the route is never re-evaluated even if the ext_proc server sets `clear_route_cache: true`.\n\n3. **Timeout response code:** Write a test that configures a short `message_timeout` and a deliberately slow ext_proc server. Verify the downstream response is `504 Gateway Timeout` (not `500`).\n\n4. **Observability mode deferred close:** Test that after an HTTP transaction completes, the gRPC stream to the ext_proc server remains open for the configured `deferred_close_timeout` duration and then closes cleanly.\n\n### Canary Deployment\n\nBefore rolling out v1.31 to production:\n\n1. Deploy Envoy v1.31 in a canary environment with a shadow copy of production traffic.\n2. Monitor ext_proc-related stats: `ext_proc.message_timeouts`, `ext_proc.streams_failed`, `ext_proc.clear_route_cache_ignored`, `ext_proc.clear_route_cache_disabled`.\n3. Check your tracing backend for newly appearing ext_proc spans and verify they are correctly parented.\n4. Verify that any `504` responses attributed to ext_proc timeouts are correctly reflected in your monitoring.\n\n### Load Testing\n\nIf you use `observability_mode`, perform load tests that create high request throughput, then verify that deferred streams do not accumulate to the point of exhausting gRPC connections or file descriptors. Tune `deferred_close_timeout` accordingly.\n\n---\n\n## Rollback Guidance\n\nIf issues occur after upgrading to v1.31.0, follow these steps to revert:\n\n### Immediate Rollback (Configuration Only)\n\nThe v1.31 ext_proc filter configuration is largely backward-compatible with v1.30 behavior:\n- `route_cache_action: DEFAULT` behaves identically to `disable_clear_route_cache: false` from v1.30 \u2014 this is the default and requires no change.\n- The `deferred_close_timeout` and `route_cache_action` fields are unknown to v1.30 and will cause a validation error if you downgrade Envoy binary without removing them from the config.\n\n**Before downgrading the Envoy binary:**\n1. Remove `route_cache_action` from your configuration and restore `disable_clear_route_cache` if needed.\n2. Remove `deferred_close_timeout` from your configuration.\n3. Regenerate gRPC stubs from the v1.30 proto files for your ext_proc server.\n4. Revert `ImmediateResponse.body` back to `string` in your ext_proc server code.\n\n### Binary Rollback\n\n1. Stop the Envoy v1.31 process.\n2. Restore the v1.30 Envoy binary.\n3. Restore the previous configuration (without v1.31-specific fields).\n4. Restart.\n\n### Timeout Error Code Rollback\n\nThe `504` vs `500` behavior change for ext_proc timeouts cannot be reverted via configuration in v1.31. If downstream clients require `500` for compatibility reasons, you will need to stay on v1.30 or handle the translation in a downstream filter or proxy layer.\n\n### Tracing Header Propagation Rollback\n\nThe gRPC tracing header propagation change also cannot be disabled via configuration in v1.31. If this causes issues (e.g., unexpected tracing headers breaking your ext_proc server), you will need to update your ext_proc server to tolerate unknown headers, or revert to v1.30.\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Changes\n\n| Category | Change | Impact |\n|----------|--------|--------|\n| **Breaking** | `ImmediateResponse.body`: `string` \u2192 `bytes` | Requires ext_proc server code update and stub regeneration |\n| **Deprecated** | `disable_clear_route_cache` superseded by `route_cache_action` | Migrate to `route_cache_action: RETAIN`; both still work but setting both is not allowed |\n| **New Field** | `route_cache_action` (enum: DEFAULT/CLEAR/RETAIN) on `ExternalProcessor` | Optional; replaces `disable_clear_route_cache` with richer semantics |\n| **New Field** | `deferred_close_timeout` on `ExternalProcessor` | Required tuning when using `observability_mode: true` |\n| **Behavior** | Observability mode fully implemented with deferred stream management | Stable for production use; configure `deferred_close_timeout` |\n| **Behavior** | Ext_proc timeout errors return `504` instead of `500` | Update alerting, SLOs, and integration tests |\n| **Behavior** | gRPC tracing context headers now propagated to ext_proc service | Verify tracing integration; update ext_proc server if needed |\n",
